longRunningSink, ev, omitStages)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tev.Stage = auditinternal.StageResponseComplete\n\t\t\tif ev.ResponseStatus == nil {\n\t\t\t\tev.ResponseStatus = fakedSuccessStatus\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tprocessAuditEvent(ctx, sink, ev, omitStages)\n\t\t}()\n\t\thandler.ServeHTTP(respWriter, req)\n\t})\n}\n\n// evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent is responsible for evaluating the audit\n// policy configuration applicable to the request and create a new audit\n// event that will be written to the API audit log.\n// - error if anything bad happened\nfunc evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent(req *http.Request, policy audit.PolicyRuleEvaluator) (*audit.AuditContext, error) {\n\tctx := req.Context()\n\tac := audit.AuditContextFrom(ctx)\n\tif ac == nil {\n\t\t// Auditing not configured.\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tattribs, err := GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn ac, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to GetAuthorizerAttributes: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\n\trac := policy.EvaluatePolicyRule(attribs)\n\taudit.ObservePolicyLevel(ctx, rac.Level)\n\tac.RequestAuditConfig = rac\n\tif rac.Level == auditinternal.LevelNone {\n\t\t// Don't audit.\n\t\treturn ac, nil\n\t}\n\n\trequestReceivedTimestamp, ok := request.ReceivedTimestampFrom(ctx)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\trequestReceivedTimestamp = time.Now()\n\t}\n\taudit.LogRequestMetadata(ctx, req, requestReceivedTimestamp, rac.Level, attribs)\n\n\treturn ac, nil\n}\n\n// writeLatencyToAnnotation writes the latency incurred in different\n// layers of the apiserver to the annotations of the audit object.\n// it should be invoked after ev.StageTimestamp has been set appropriately.\nfunc writeLatencyToAnnotation(ctx context.Context, ev *auditinternal.Event) {\n\t// we will track latency in annotation only when the total latency\n\t// of the given request exceeds 500ms, this is in keeping with the\n\t// traces in rest/handlers for create, delete, update,\n\t// get, list, and deletecollection.\n\tconst threshold = 500 * time.Millisecond\n\tlatency := ev.StageTimestamp.Time.Sub(ev.RequestReceivedTimestamp.Time)\n\tif latency <= threshold {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// if we are tracking latency incurred inside different layers within\n\t// the apiserver, add these as annotation to the audit event object.\n\tlayerLatencies := request.AuditAnnotationsFromLatencyTrackers(ctx)\n\tif len(layerLatencies) == 0 {\n\t\t// latency tracking is not enabled for this request\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// record the total latency for this request, for convenience.\n\tlayerLatencies[\"apiserver.latency.k8s.io/total\"] = latency.String()\n\taudit.AddAuditAnnotationsMap(ctx, layerLatencies)\n}\n\nfunc processAuditEvent(ctx context.Context, sink audit.Sink, ev *auditinternal.Event, omitStages []auditinternal.Stage) bool {\n\tfor _, stage := range omitStages {\n\t\tif ev.Stage == stage {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tswitch {\n\tcase ev.Stage == auditinternal.StageRequestReceived:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(ev.RequestReceivedTimestamp.Time)\n\tcase ev.Stage == auditinternal.StageResponseComplete:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(time.Now())\n\t\twriteLatencyToAnnotation(ctx, ev)\n\tdefault:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(time.Now())\n\t}\n\n\taudit.ObserveEvent(ctx)\n\treturn sink.ProcessEvents(ev)\n}\n\nfunc decorateResponseWriter(ctx context.Context, responseWriter http.ResponseWriter, ev *auditinternal.Event, sink audit.Sink, omitStages []auditinternal.Stage) http.ResponseWriter {\n\tdelegate := &auditResponseWriter{\n\t\tctx:            ctx,\n\t\tResponseWriter: &auditResponseWriter{}\nvar _ responsewriter.UserProvidedDecorator = &auditResponseWriter{}\n\n// auditResponseWriter intercepts WriteHeader, sets it in the event. If the sink is set, it will\n// create immediately an event (for long running requests).\ntype auditResponseWriter struct {\n\thttp.ResponseWriter\n\tctx        context.Context\n\tevent      *auditinternal.Event\n\tonce       sync.Once\n\tsink       audit.Sink\n\tomitStages []auditinternal.Stage\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Unwrap() http.ResponseWriter {\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) processCode(code int) {\n\ta.once.Do(func() {\n\t\tif a.event.ResponseStatus == nil {\n\t\t\ta.event.ResponseStatus = &metav1.Status{}\n\t\t}\n\t\ta.event.ResponseStatus.Code = int32(code)\n\t\ta.event.Stage = auditinternal.StageResponseStarted\n\n\t\tif a.sink != nil {\n\t\t\tprocessAuditEvent(a.ctx, a.sink, a.event, a.omitStages)\n\t\t}\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Write(bs []byte) (int, error) {\n\t// the Go library calls WriteHeader internally if no code was written yet. But this will go unnoticed for us\n\ta.processCode(http.StatusOK)\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter.Write(bs)\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) WriteHeader(code int) {\n\ta.processCode(code)\n\ta.ResponseWriter.WriteHeader(code)\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Hijack() (net.Conn, *bufio.ReadWriter, error) {\n\t// fake a response status before protocol switch happens\n\ta.processCode(http.StatusSwitchingProtocols)\n\n\t// the outer ResponseWriter object returned by WrapForHTTP1Or2 implements\n\t// http.Hijacker if the inner object (a.ResponseWriter) implements http.Hijacker.\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter.(http.Hijacker).Hijack()\n}\n","numLines":264,"startLine":1,"totalLines":264}}}

    p.OmitStages,\n    78→\t\tOmitManagedFields: p.OmitManagedFields,\n    79→\t}\n    80→}\n    81→\n    82→// isOmitManagedFields returns whether to omit managed fields from the request\n    83→// and response bodies from being written to the API audit log.\n    84→// If a user specifies OmitManagedFields inside a policy rule, that overrides\n    85→// the global policy default in 148→}\n   149→\n   150→// Check whether the path matches the path specification.\n   151→func pathMatches(path, spec string) bool {\n   152→\t// Allow wildcard match\n   153→\tif spec == \"*\" {\n   154→\t\treturn true\n   155→\t}\n   156→\t// Allow exact match\n   157→\tif spec == path {\n   158→\t\treturn true\n   159→\t}\n   160→\t// Allow a trailing * subpath match\n   161→\tif If the specified auditID is empty, no value is set.\nfunc WithAuditID(ctx context.Context, auditID types.UID) {\n\tif auditID == \"\" {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tif ac := AuditContextFrom(ctx); ac != nil {\n\t\tac.Event.AuditID = auditID\n\t}\n}\n\n// AuditIDFrom returns the value of the audit ID from the request context, along with whether\n// auditing is enabled.\nfunc AuditIDFrom(ctx context.Context) (types.UID, bool) {\n\tif ac := AuditContextFrom(ctx); ac != nil {\n\t\treturn ac.Event.AuditID, true\n\t}\n\treturn \"\", false\n}\n\n// GetAuditIDTruncated returns the audit ID (truncated) from the request context.\n// If the length of the Audit-ID value exceeds the limit, we truncate it to keep\n// the first N (maxAuditIDLength) characters.\n// This is intended to be used in logging only.\nfunc GetAuditIDTruncated(ctx context.Context) string {\n\tauditID, ok := AuditIDFrom(ctx)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\t// if the user has specified a very long audit ID then we will use the first N characters\n\t// Note: assuming Audit-ID header is in ASCII\n\tconst maxAuditIDLength = 64\n\tif len(auditID) > maxAuditIDLength {\n\t\tauditID = auditID[:maxAuditIDLength]\n\t}\n\n\treturn string(auditID)\n}\n","numLines":189,"startLine":1,"totalLines":189}}}

Kubernetes API server audit logging system is implemented across multiple packages in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`. Here are the key components:\\n\\n### 1. Audit Event Creation from Requests\\n\\nAudit event creation starts when HTTP requests reach the API server:\\n\\n- **Request Flow Initialization** (`audit_init.go`): The `WithAuditInit` filter initializes the audit context and generates or echoes the Audit-ID header.\\n\\n- **Audit Event Creation** (`audit.go`): The `WithAudit` filter is the main entry point that decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to create audit events from incoming requests.\\n\\n- **Authentication Audit** (`authn_audit.go`): The `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` filter handles audit logging for failed authentication attempts.\\n\\n- **Metadata Logging** (`request.go`): Functions like `LogRequestMetadata`, `LogRequestObject`, and `LogResponseObject` populate audit event fields with request and response details. The `LogRequestMetadata` function extracts user information, verb, URI, source IPs, and object references from incoming requests.\\n\\n- **Audit Context** (`context.go`): The `AuditContext` type stores the audit event being captured and the evaluated policy configuration. Functions like `WithAuditContext`, `AuditContextFrom`, and `AddAuditAnnotation` manage the audit context through the request lifecycle.\\n\\n### 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies determine which requests should be audited and at what level:\\n\\n- **Policy Evaluator Interface** (`evaluator.go`): The `PolicyRuleEvaluator` interface defines the `EvaluatePolicyRule` method that evaluates audit policies against request attributes.\\n\\n- **Policy Rule Matching** (`checker.go`): The `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` function creates a policy evaluator instance. The `EvaluatePolicyRule` method matches requests against audit policy rules by checking users, user groups, verbs, namespaces, resources, and non-resource URLs. The `ruleMatches` function implements the matching logic.\\n\\n- **Policy Loading** (`reader.go`): The `LoadPolicyFromFile` and `LoadPolicyFromBytes` functions load audit policies from YAML configuration files. Policies define the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and which stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic) to audit.\\n\\n### 3. Audit Backend Dispatch (Log File vs Webhook)\\n\\nAudit backends handle the actual storage and transmission of audit events:\\n\\n- **Backend Interface** (`types.go`): The `Backend` interface defines the contract for audit backends, with methods `ProcessEvents`, `Run`, and `Shutdown`. The `Sink` interface is the minimal interface for processing events.\\n\\n- **Log File Backend** (`log/backend.go`): The `NewBackend` function creates a file-based audit backend. The `ProcessEvents` method writes audit events to a file in either legacy text format or JSON format.\\n\\n- **Webhook Backend** (`webhook/webhook.go`): The `NewBackend` function creates an HTTP webhook backend that sends audit events to an external service. The `ProcessEvents` method batches events and sends them via HTTP POST with exponential backoff retry logic.\\n\\n- **Union Backend** (`union.go`): The `Union` function creates a composite backend that dispatches audit events to multiple backends (both log file and webhook). It processes events through each backend in sequence.\\n\\n- **Buffered Backend** (`buffered/buffered.go`): The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend with buffering and batching capabilities. Events are buffered in a channel and sent in batches with configurable batch size, wait time, and rate limiting.\\n\\n- **Backend Configuration** (`server/options/audit.go`): The `ApplyTo` method in AuditOptions orchestrates backend creation and dispatch setup. It builds the policy evaluator, creates log and webhook backends, applies truncation wrapping, and combines them using the Union backend.\\n\\n### 4. Audit Truncation for Large Request/Response Bodies\\n\\nTruncation prevents audit events from becoming too large:\\n\\n- **Truncate Backend** (`truncate/truncate.go`): The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend with truncation logic. The `ProcessEvents` method calculates event sizes, and if an event exceeds `MaxEventSize`, the `truncate` function removes the RequestObject and ResponseObject fields, keeping only metadata. Events are also batched to not exceed `MaxBatchSize`.\\n\\n### 5. Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n- **Managed Fields Handling** (`request.go`): The `copyWithoutManagedFields` function removes Kubernetes-managed fields from request and response bodies before auditing, as controlled by the `OmitManagedFields` policy option.\\n\\n- **Event Formatting** (`format.go`): The `EventString` function creates single-line text representations of audit events for the legacy log format.\\n\\n- **Metrics** (`metrics.go`): The audit subsystem tracks event counters, error rates, and other audit-related metrics.\\n\\n- **Admission Audit** (`admission/audit.go`): The `WithAudit` decorator wraps admission controllers to capture their annotations in the audit event.\\n\\nThe audit logging system follows a pipeline architecture where events flow through: initialization → policy evaluation → metadata logging → backend dispatch → optional truncation → final storage/transmission.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1795,"cache_read_input_tokens":64312,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1795},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"51303832-b356-4796-a918-3a5d9569295d","uuid":"6987c826-8cd4-4501-a128-ebbfa376545f"}

The `ProcessEvents` method batches events and sends them via HTTP POST with exponential backoff retry logic.\\n\\n- **Union Backend** (`union.go`): The `Union` function creates a composite backend that dispatches audit events to multiple backends (both log file and webhook). It processes events through each backend in sequence.\\n\\n- **Buffered Backend** (`buffered/buffered.go`): The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend with buffering and batching capabilities. Events are buffered in a channel and sent in batches with configurable batch size, wait time, and rate limiting.\\n\\n- **Backend Configuration** (`server/options/audit.go`): The `ApplyTo` method in AuditOptions orchestrates backend creation and dispatch setup. It builds the policy evaluator, creates log and webhook backends, applies truncation wrapping, and combines them using the Union backend.\\n\\n### 4. Audit Truncation for Large Request/Response Bodies\\n\\nTruncation prevents audit events from becoming too large:\\n\\n- **Truncate Backend** (`truncate/truncate.go`): The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend with truncation logic. The `ProcessEvents` method calculates event sizes, and if an event exceeds `MaxEventSize`, the `truncate` function removes the RequestObject and ResponseObject fields, keeping only metadata. Events are also batched to not exceed `MaxBatchSize`.\\n\\n### 5. Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n- **Managed Fields Handling** (`request.go`): The `copyWithoutManagedFields` function removes Kubernetes-managed fields from request and response bodies before auditing, as controlled by the `OmitManagedFields` policy option.\\n\\n- **Event Formatting** (`format.go`): The `EventString` function creates single-line text representations of audit events for the legacy log format.\\n\\n- **Metrics** (`metrics.go`): The audit subsystem tracks event counters, error rates, and other audit-related metrics.\\n\\n- **Admission Audit** (`admission/audit.go`): The `WithAudit` decorator wraps admission controllers to capture their annotations in the audit event.\\n\\nThe audit logging system follows a pipeline architecture where events flow through: initialization → policy evaluation → metadata logging → backend dispatch → optional truncation → final storage/transmission.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
